9:04 PM EDT</div></div><div class="article-body"><div class="teaser-content"><section><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The House committees leading the impeachment inquiry requested a long list of documents and communications Friday from Vice President Pence related to Ukraine.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Earlier, President Trump said that Democrats “unfortunately have the votes” to impeach him in the House, but he predicted he would “win” in a trial in the Republican-led Senate.</p></div></section></div><div class="remainder-content"><section><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“The Republicans are very unified,” Trump said, as he again insisted he had said nothing inappropriate during the July call in which he pressed Ukrainian President Volodymyr Zelensky to investigate former vice president Joe Biden and his son Hunter Biden.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump’s comments to reporters at the White House came as fallout continued Friday from the late-night release of text messages by House investigators, while another key figure, the inspector general of the intelligence community, testified on Capitol Hill behind closed doors.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The texts released late Thursday show how State Department officials coordinated with Zelensky’s top aide and Trump’s personal lawyer Rudolph W. Giuliani to leverage a potential summit between Trump and Zelensky on a promise from the Ukrainians to investigate an energy company, Burisma, that had employed Hunter Biden.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Early Friday, Ukraine’s chief prosecutor said he would conduct an “audit” of an investigation related to Burisma.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">●Trump publicly calls on China <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-publicly-calls-on-china-to-investigate-bidens/2019/10/03/2ae94f6a-e5f2-11e9-b403-f738899982d2_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_10">to investigate Bidens</a></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">●Trump’s removal would require Republican dissidents. But those who speak out <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trumps-removal-would-require-republican-dissidents-but-those-who-speak-out-become-targets-of-viral-disinformation/2019/10/03/35c35ad0-e394-11e9-b403-f738899982d2_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_11">become targets</a> of viral disinformation.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">●Trump wanted Ukraine’s president to launch investigations before face-to-face meeting, State Department <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/this-is-when-the-inquiry-gets-real-former-us-special-envoy-to-ukraine-testifies-in-impeachment-probe-today/2019/10/03/51365c1b-5a01-4e44-872a-299b67949a5e_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_12">texts show</a></p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_2"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/context/read-the-whistleblower-complaint-regarding-president-trump-s-communications-with-ukrainian-president-volodymyr-zelensky/4b9e0ca5-3824-467f-b1a3-77f2d4ee16aa/?tid=lk_inline_manual_14" title="www.washingtonpost.com">Read the whistleblower complaint </a>| <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/context/official-readout-president-trump-s-july-25-phone-call-with-ukraine-s-volodymyr-zelensky/4b228f51-17e7-45bc-b16c-3b2643f3fbe0/?tid=lk_inline_manual_14" title="www.washingtonpost.com">The rough transcript of Trump’s call with Zelensky </a> <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/09/30/trump-impeachment/?tid=lk_inline_manual_14" title="www.washingtonpost.com">House Democrats’ letter on State Department texts</a></p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_2"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>6:40 p.m.: Defense Secretary Mark Esper declines to give details of delay in aid to Ukraine</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Defense Secretary Mark Esper declined to say whether or how Pentagon officials had addressed the delay in providing military aid to Ukraine after they informed Congress this spring that the country had made sufficient progress on corruption to receive it.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“I’m not going to add any fuel to the fire at this point in time,” Esper told reporters traveling with him to Kentucky and Ohio. He said the Defense Department would answer any congressional questions if they arose.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_3"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Right now I’m trying to keep DOD out of this issue,” he said. “It’s a very political issue.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Esper said “the good news” was that officials had wanted to ensure that the aid went forward by the end of the year, and that was now occurring. This week the State Department said it was approving the sale of $39 million in Javelin missiles to Ukraine.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_3"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">– <i>Missy Ryan</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>6:20 p.m.: House committee chairmen send a subpoena to the White House</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Chairmen of the House Oversight, Intelligence and Foreign Affairs committees issued a subpoena to White House acting chief of staff Mick Mulvaney for documents as part of the impeachment inquiry into Trump. The letter compels Mulvaney to produce the records by Oct. 18.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_4"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Your failure or refusal to comply with the subpoena, including at the direction or behest of the President or others at the White House, shall constitute evidence of obstruction of the House’s impeachment inquiry and may be used as an adverse inference against you and the President,” wrote chairmen Elijah E. Cummings (D-Md.), Adam B. Schiff (D-Calif.) and Eliot Engel (D-N.Y.).</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The letter says House committee chairmen twice asked the White House for documents related to the investigation and the White House did not produce the records or reply to the requests. The congressmen referenced news reporting that Trump plans to write a letter to Speaker Nancy Pelosi saying the White House will not cooperate with the impeachment inquiry until there is a vote on the House floor.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_4"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“We deeply regret that President Trump has put us — and the nation — in this position, but his actions have left us with no choice but to issue this subpoena,” the chairmen wrote.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_5"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>5:40 p.m.: Trump references impeachment in a speech at the White House</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Speaking to young black conservatives at the White House, Trump said congressional Democrats and “the corrupt forces in Washington” were trying to suppress the voices of voters.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“They’re trying to steal your vote, they’re trying to steal your voice and they’re trying to steal your country,” he told attendees at the Young Black Leadership Summit organized by conservative nonprofit Turning Point USA. “They don’t have what it takes.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The oblique reference to impeachment came amid a wide-ranging speech that hit on criminal justice reform, school choice, the U.S.-Mexico border and free speech on college campuses, among other topics. Pence also appeared at the event, although he did not speak.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_5"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_6"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>5:30 p.m.: Schiff thanks Atkinson for testifying before the House Intelligence Committee</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In a statement released after intelligence community inspector general Michael Atkinson’s closed-door testimony, Schiff said the committee had explored with Atkinson why he had found the whistleblower complaint about the Ukraine call to be “urgent and credible.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Now that we have all seen the call record, we can see that the IG’s determination was correct in both respects,” Schiff said. “That call record shows that Trump pressured a foreign leader to interfere in the 2020 election by investigating a political opponent. Those facts cannot be seriously contested.”</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_7"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Schiff said the committee’s Republicans had argued that because the whistleblower reached out to the committee for guidance, the committee could not investigate the complaint.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_6"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“If that were true, no whistleblower could contact Congress, and no committee could conduct an investigation,” Schiff said. “We look forward to following up on what we learned today and continuing our investigation into the facts.”</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>5:20 p.m.: Biden says no conflict of interest for son to work for foreign company</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Biden became defensive when asked by a reporter whether his son’s job in Ukraine gave even the appearance of a conflict of interest.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“It’s not a conflict of interest. There’s been no indication of any conflict of interest … Period. I’m not going to-” Biden said.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_8"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The reporter interjected, “But even the appearance of conflict of interest?”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“I’m not going to respond to that,” Biden replied. “Focus on this man. What he’s doing that no president has ever done. No president.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">—<span> Amy Wang</span></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>4:30 p.m.: Utah Democrat’s support for impeachment inquiry leaves just 9 Democrats not on board </b></p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_7"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Rep. Ben Adams’s decision Friday to back the House Democrats’ impeachment probe brings the number of Democrats who don’t support it into single digits.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">McAdams is the 88th House Democrat to come on board for an inquiry in the last two weeks since the news broke of Trump’s call with the Ukrainian president.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">At an event in his district, Adams was pressed on the subject and <a href="https://www.sltrib.com/news/politics/2019/10/04/rep-ben-mcadams-says/" title="www.sltrib.com">he told</a> constituents, “I am not on the fence.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“The president’s refusal to further cooperate with congressional oversight, without an impeachment inquiry, is regrettable,” McAdams said in his updated comments. “We find ourselves today at the point that an [impeachment] inquiry is necessary to get all of the facts on the table.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The remaining nine Democratic holdouts hail from conservative districts that voted for Trump.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>3:30 p.m.: House committees request information from Pence</b></p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_8"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The committees leading the impeachment inquiry sent <a href="https://oversight.house.gov/sites/democrats.oversight.house.gov/files/documents/2019-10-04.EEC%20Engel%20Schiff%20%20re%20Request%20to%20VP%2010-04-19%20Letter%20and%20Schedule.pdf" title="oversight.house.gov">a letter</a> to Pence asking for an expansive list of documents and communications to determine Pence’s knowledge of Trump asking Ukraine to investigate Biden.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Recently, public reports have raised questions about any role you may have played in conveying or reinforcing the President’s stark message to the Ukrainian President,” the letter reads.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">It specifically points to news reports that a member of Pence’s staff may have been on the call between Trump and Zelensky, and to Pence’s meeting with the Ukrainian president in September.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">They are also seeking all communication — “including but not limited to requests, suggestions, proposals, or other communications” — around Trump’s decision not to send Pence to the Ukrainian president’s inauguration in May as well as a call Pence had with Zelensky in September.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>1:50 p.m.: China vows not to ‘interfere’ after Trump asks for Biden probe</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Chinese Foreign Minister Wang Yi said Friday that China “will not interfere in the internal affairs of the U.S.,” after President Trump urged Beijing to probe his political rival Joe Biden amid an impeachment inquiry in Washington.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“We trust that the American people will be able to sort out their own problems,” the Global Times, a party-affiliated newspaper, reported Wang as saying.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Read more <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2019/10/04/china-vows-not-interfere-after-trump-asks-biden-probe/?tid=lk_inline_manual_76" title="www.washingtonpost.com">here</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Siobhan O’Grady</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>1:40 p.m.: Rubio plays down Trump’s China ask, says it wasn’t a ‘real request’</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">When asked if it was appropriate for Trump to ask China to investigate Biden, Sen. Marco Rubio (R-Fla.) said Trump didn’t really mean it.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“I don’t know if that’s a real request or him just needling the press knowing you guys were going to get outraged by it. He’s pretty good at getting everyone fired up and the media responded right on task,” Rubio said, <a href="https://twitter.com/DeFede/status/1180166630803939330" title="twitter.com">according to video posted</a> to Twitter.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Asked again if it’s all right for Trump to say that, Rubio repeated his dismissal of it.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“I don’t think it’s a real request. Again, I think he did it to gig you guys. . . . I think he did it to provoke you to ask me and others and get outraged by it. Like I said, he plays it like a violin and everybody falls right in. That’s not a real request.”</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>1:15 p.m.: Biden says his family knows ‘what real pain is,’ Hunter will be a part of his campaign</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Biden defended his son against Trump’s attacks, telling the Reno Gazette Journal <a href="https://www.rgj.com/story/news/2019/10/03/joe-biden-2020-campaign-trail-defends-son-against-donald-trump-remarks/3849550002/" title="www.rgj.com">in an interview</a> that Hunter Biden is “a fine man” who has “been through hell.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">He also said Hunter will play a role in his presidential campaign.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Biden said he understands that these attacks are just the beginning of going up against Trump, but that he is not deterred.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Look, we are a family. We have been through a lot worse,” Biden said. “We know what real pain is.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Biden’s wife and infant daughter were killed in a car accident in 1972 when his sons were young. His oldest son, Beau Biden, died in 2015 of brain cancer.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>1 p.m.: Volker defended Biden to Congress against Trump accusations of corruption </b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Kurt Volker, the former U.S. special representative for Ukraine, defended Biden in his opening statement to Congress on Thursday and said he was trying to run interference on information being supplied to Trump by Giuliani to secure continued American support for the government in Ukraine.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Volker said he did not believe allegations that Giuliani has leveled against Joe Biden, namely that Biden was influenced in his dealings with the Ukrainian leadership by his son’s presence on the board of a Ukrainian gas company whose owner was being investigated by authorities in Kiev.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“I have known former vice president Biden for 24 years, and the suggestion that he would be influenced in his duties as vice president by money for his son simply has no credibility to me,” Volker said. “I know him as a man of integrity and dedication to our country.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Volker sought to present himself in the testimony as a man caught in the middle of Giuliani’s efforts to pressure the Ukrainian leadership for Trump’s domestic political purposes and Ukrainian President Volodymyr Zelensky’s attempts to maintain U.S. support for Ukraine and win a meeting with Trump.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Paul Sonne and Greg Jaffe </i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>12:20 p.m.: Romney criticizes Trump’s ‘brazen and unprecedented’ appeals to Ukraine, China</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Sen. Mitt Romney (R-Utah) on Friday condemned Trump’s efforts to get Ukraine and China to investigate the Bidens as “wrong and appalling,” breaking ranks with most Republicans on Capitol Hill who have largely avoided criticizing the president.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In a pair of tweets, Romney referenced that fact that Biden is running for president.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“When the only American citizen President Trump singles out for China’s investigation is his political opponent in the midst of the Democratic nomination process, it strains credulity to suggest that it is anything other than politically motivated,” Romney said in <a href="https://twitter.com/MittRomney/status/1180151212030779392">one tweet</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“By all appearances, the President’s brazen and unprecedented appeal to China and to Ukraine to investigate Joe Biden is wrong and appalling,” he added in <a href="https://twitter.com/MittRomney/status/1180151213993730049">another</a>.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>12:05 p.m.: E.U. Ambassador Gordon Sondland gave $1 million to Trump inaugural committee through LLCs</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Gordon Sondland, the U.S. ambassador to the European Union who has become <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/nation/2019/10/04/gordon-sondland-ukraine-texts-ambassador/?tid=lk_inline_manual_106">a key figure in the Ukraine controversy</a>, has been a longtime donor to the Republican Party, previously supporting the presidential campaigns of George W. Bush and Mitt Romney.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In the 2016 primaries, he initially supported Jeb Bush’s campaign and the super PAC supporting Jeb Bush.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">When Trump became the party’s presumptive nominee, Sondland signed on to the joint finance operation between the campaign and the party as a major fundraiser, or a “bundler” who collects big checks on behalf of the nominee.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Sondland was announced as the Oregon and Washington state co-chair of Trump Victory in July 2016. He was listed as a co-host of an August 2016 fundraiser in Seattle in his capacity as Trump Victory co-chair, according to an invitation. Tickets for that fundraisers cost as high as $100,000 per couple.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">But once media outlets reported plans for that fundraiser, Sondland and another Portland hotelier, Bashar Wali, said their names were added without their approval and declined to participate as co-hosts, the Willamette Week reported at the time. The two men said through a Provenance Hotels spokeswoman that they refused to participate due to Trump’s anti-immigrant stance.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Sondland eventually donated $1 million to Trump’s inaugural committee through four limited-liability companies, state and federal records show. Buena Vista Investments LLC and BV-2 LLC gave $350,000 each, and Dunson Cornerstone Inc. and Dunson Investments LLC gave $150,000 each, inaugural committee records show.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">All four companies are registered in Washington, under Sondland’s name. Sondland was among at least 47 people or corporations who gave $1 million or more to the Trump inaugural committee, which drew $107 million. Sondland’s donations were first reported in 2017 by the Intercept, the Center for Responsive Politics and other outlets.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Michelle Ye Hee Lee</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>12 p.m.: Cornyn tweets that Justice is investigating Biden ‘conflicts of interest’</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Sen. John Cornyn (R-Tex.) tweeted Friday morning that the Justice Department is “investigating foreign government influence, VP Biden conflicts of interest, and possible corruption.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">A spokesman for Cornyn clarified that the senator was referring to the ongoing investigation being conducted by U.S. Attorney John Durham into various activities surrounding the FBI’s Russia probe and that “the Durham investigation could end up also looking at the Bidens.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">A spokeswoman for the Justice Department did not immediately respond to messages, and an FBI spokeswoman declined to comment.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">When asked by a reporter later Friday morning if the Justice Department was looking into Biden, Trump said, “Well, that you’d have to ask Attorney General Barr, but I can tell you just as an observer that what I saw Biden do with his son, he’s pillaging these countries, and he’s hurting us.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The Biden family’s Ukraine dealings would seem far afield of what has been publicly revealed about Durham’s work. When it was first announced that Barr had tapped Durham to conduct the review, a person familiar with the matter said the prosecutor was seeking to determine if the U.S. government’s “intelligence collection activities” related to the Trump campaign were “lawful and appropriate.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">A Justice Department spokeswoman said more recently that Durham was “exploring the extent to which a number of countries, including Ukraine, played a role in the counterintelligence investigation directed at the Trump campaign during the 2016 election.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“While the Attorney General has yet to contact Ukraine in connection with this investigation, certain Ukrainians who are not members of the government have volunteered information to Mr. Durham, which he is evaluating,” the spokeswoman said.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Matt Zapotosky</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>11:45 a.m.: Trump won’t say whether he’s asked countries to investigate any nonpolitical opponents</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Speaking to reporters at the White House on Friday, Trump said he didn’t know if he had ever asked a foreign leader to investigate a person who wasn’t his political opponent, though he said he had a right to do so.</p></div><div><figure class="pad-top-xs mb-md ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns center hide-for-print"><div class="powa-wrapper"><div class="powa-skip" data-ad-bar="1" data-aspect-ratio="0.5625" data-blurb="true" data-org="wapo" data-playthrough="true" data-uuid="b28d8949-cefd-436a-bb5d-8e0cac038ef2"></div></div></figure></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“You know, we would have to look,” Trump said. “But what I looked for and will always ask for is anything having to do with corruption.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Reporters asked him several times if that included enlisting Russian President Vladimir Putin’s help, but Trump ignored the question.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“I’ll tell you what’s okay,” he continued. “If we feel there is corruption, we have a right to go to a foreign country.”</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>11:30 a.m.: Trump says Democrats have votes to impeach him in House</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump told reporters Friday that it appears House Democrats have the votes to impeach him but predicted that he would be acquitted in a trial in the Republican-led Senate.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“The Democrats unfortunately, they have the votes,” Trump said as he prepared to leave the White House. “They can vote very easily, even though most of them, many of them, don’t believe they should do it.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“If they proceed, they’ll just get their people, they’re all in line, even though many of them don’t want to vote, they have no choice,” Trump added. “They have to follow their leadership. And then we’ll get it to the Senate, and we’re going to win. The Republicans have been very unified.”</p></div><div><figure class="pad-top-xs mb-md ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns center hide-for-print"><div class="powa-wrapper"><div class="powa-skip" data-ad-bar="1" data-aspect-ratio="0.5625" data-blurb="true" data-org="wapo" data-playthrough="true" data-uuid="ba8ba6cd-a9bc-42f0-b465-63a91fb33ef7"></div></div></figure></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump said Democrats would “pay a tremendous price at the polls” for impeaching him.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">He continued to insist that he had done nothing inappropriate during his July call in which he pressed Zelensky to investigate the Bidens.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“When I speak to a foreign leader, I speak in an appropriate manner,” Trump said.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>10:30 a.m.: Trump shares purported employer of whistleblower in a tweet</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In the midst of several midmorning tweets, Trump identified the purported employer of the whistleblower as the CIA.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In the tweet, Trump quoted longtime Republican operative Ed Rollins from an appearance on Fox News.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“I think it’s outrages that a Whistleblower is a CIA Agent,” <a href="https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1180123504924151809">Trump quoted</a> Rollins as saying, misspelling “outrageous.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Federal laws offer only limited protection for those in the intelligence community who report wrongdoing — even when they follow all the rules for doing so.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“If he wants to destroy this person’s life, there’s not a lot to stop him right now,” whistleblower attorney Bradley P. Moss told The Washington Post last week.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Both The Post and the New York Times have published stories identifying the whistleblower as a CIA officer, drawing objections from the whistleblower’s lawyers, who say he is entitled to anonymity under the law.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>10 a.m.: Trump camp to air anti-Biden ads in key early primary states</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Beginning this weekend, the Trump campaign is airing more than $1 million worth of TV ads in early primary states that accuse Joe Biden and his son Hunter of corruption in Ukraine, according to Brad Parscale, Trump’s campaign manager.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The commercials will air in Iowa, New Hampshire, South Carolina and Nevada, Parscale tweeted.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The anti-Biden ads are part of a larger $8 million ad buy focused on impeachment, which the Trump camp is trying to spin to its advantage.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">CNN said Thursday it would not run the ad because the allegations of corruption against the Bidens highlighted in the ad are unsubstantiated.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>9:50 a.m.: Intelligence community inspector general meeting with Congress about whistleblower complaint</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Atkinson will appear before the House Intelligence Committee on Friday to discuss the complaint from a whistleblower that touched off the impeachment probe against Trump.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">He arrived on Capitol Hill shortly before 10 a.m. for a scheduled 10:30 a.m. hearing.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The hearing is necessary “to establish additional details, leads and evidence” in the probe, Schiff, the House Intelligence Committee chairman, wrote in a letter to colleagues last week. The hearing will not be public.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy hide-for-print ma-0 mb-md interstitial italic"><a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/local/legal-issues/ig-at-center-of-impeachment-inquiry-promised-robust-whistleblower-protections-when-he-took-job/2019/10/03/8e8c73e2-e554-11e9-a6e8-8759c5c7f608_story.html?tid=lk_interstitial_manual_159">IG at center of impeachment inquiry promised robust whistleblower protections when he took job</a></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“We have to flesh out all of the facts for the American people. The seriousness of the matter and the danger to our country demands nothing less,” Schiff wrote.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Atkinson alerted Schiff and other congressional committee leaders to the whistleblower’s complaint last month, but at the time, acting director of national intelligence Joseph Maguire would not allow Atkinson to share the full complaint with the committees.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Read more <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/intelligence-community-inspector-general-meets-with-congress-today-about-whistleblower-complaint/2019/10/04/48e2d382-e625-11e9-a331-2df12d56a80b_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_162">here</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Shane Harris, Rachael Bade and Karoun Demirjian</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>9 a.m.: House Republicans object to White House subpoena</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Republicans on the House Oversight Committee on Friday made public a letter to Cummings, the committee’s chairman, in which they objected to his threatened subpoena of White House records related to Trump’s call with Zelensky.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“You decided to issue this subpoena without consulting Republicans and without allowing Members to debate the terms of the subpoena,” the Republicans wrote in <a href="https://republicans-oversight.house.gov/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/2019-10-03-COR-Members-to-EEC-re-Ukraine-Subpoenas.pdf">the letter</a>, dated Thursday. “Your memorandum cherry-picks and misstates information to propagate a misleading narrative about the President’s actions. We object strongly to the issuance of this subpoena and your stated reasons for issuing it.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Cummings said earlier this week he would issue a subpoena if the White House didn’t reply with document requests by Friday.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>8:50 a.m.: Trump seizes on unemployment rate in arguing against impeachment</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump seized the release of new unemployment numbers Friday morning to argue against his impeachment.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Breaking News: Unemployment Rate, at 3.5%, drops to a 50 YEAR LOW,” he <a href="https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1180102056411095042">tweeted</a>. “Wow America, lets impeach your President (even though he did nothing wrong!).”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump made no mention that the same report showed the economy adding a modest 136,000 jobs in September, in what is likely to be interpreted as further evidence that the country is headed for a slowdown.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy hide-for-print ma-0 mb-md interstitial italic"><a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/2019/10/04/us-economy-added-just-jobs-september-fresh-sign-economy-is-cooling/?tid=lk_interstitial_manual_174">U.S. economy added just 136,000 jobs in September, in fresh sign economy is cooling</a></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>8:25 a.m.: Schiff says Republicans must decide if Trump has ‘absolute right’ he claims</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In a morning <a href="https://twitter.com/RepAdamSchiff/status/1180093875144269824">tweet</a>, Schiff responded to Trump’s late-night assertion that he has an “absolute right” to enlist foreign countries in corruption investigations.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump’s contention, in a tweet, came at the end of a day in which he publicly urged both Ukraine and China to investigate the business dealings of Hunter Biden.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“It comes down to this,” Schiff tweeted. “We’ve cut through the denials. The deflections. The nonsense. Donald Trump believes he can pressure a foreign nation to help him politically. It’s his ‘right.’ Every Republican in Congress has to decide: Is he right?”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Minutes after Schiff’s tweet, Trump doubled down on his assertion.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“As President I have an obligation to end CORRUPTION, even if that means requesting the help of a foreign country or countries,” he <a href="https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1180094411323117568">tweeted</a>. “It is done all the time. This has NOTHING to do with politics or a political campaign against the Bidens. This does have to do with their corruption!”</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>6:45 a.m.: Ukraine’s new chief prosecutor to ‘audit’ Biden case</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">KIEV, Ukraine — Ukraine’s new chief prosecutor said Friday his office will conduct an “audit” of an investigation into Burisma, a Ukrainian gas company that had recruited Hunter Biden for its board.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">A criminal probe of the company was closed in 2016, and Trump has alleged it was because of pressure by Hunter Biden’s father, Joe Biden, who was then vice president. Trump has insisted that Ukraine open a new investigation.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Ukrainian officials said previously that the probe was focused on the years 2010 to 2012, before the younger Biden joined the board. They also have said that there is no evidence of any wrongdoing on his part.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Prosecutor General Ruslan Ryaboshapka told a news conference that he is aware of at least 15 investigations that may have touched on Burisma, its owner Nikolai Zlochevsky, an associate named Serhiy Zerchenko, and Biden, and that all will be reviewed. He said no foreign or Ukrainian official has been in touch with him to request this audit.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Read more <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/europe/ukraines-new-chief-prosecutor-to-audit-biden-case/2019/10/04/fce8d3fa-e68d-11e9-a6e8-8759c5c7f608_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_188">here</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Will Englund</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>6:30 a.m.: Trump wanted Ukraine’s president to launch investigations before face-to-face meeting, texts show</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">House investigators released numerous text messages late Thursday night illustrating how senior State Department officials coordinated with the Ukrainian president’s top aide and Trump’s personal lawyer to leverage a potential summit between the heads of state on a promise from the Ukrainians to investigate the 2016 U.S. election and an energy company that employed Biden’s son.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The texts, which former special U.S. envoy to Ukraine Kurt Volker provided investigators during a nearly 10-hour deposition Thursday, reveal that officials felt Trump would not agree to meet with Zelensky unless Zelensky promised to launch the investigations — and did so publicly.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Although the texts do not mention Biden by name, congressional Democrats leading an impeachment inquiry are pointing to them as clear evidence that Trump conditioned normal bilateral relations with Ukraine on that country first agreeing “to launch politically motivated investigations,” top Democrats said in a statement Thursday night.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“heard from White House — assuming President Z convinces trump he will investigate / ‘get to the bottom of what happened’ in 2016, we will nail down date for visit to Washington,” Volker texted Zelensky’s aide, Andrey Yermak, on July 25, hours before Trump and the Ukrainian president spoke via phone.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Read more <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/this-is-when-the-inquiry-gets-real-former-us-special-envoy-to-ukraine-testifies-in-impeachment-probe-today/2019/10/03/51365c1b-5a01-4e44-872a-299b67949a5e_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_196" title="www.washingtonpost.com">here</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Karoun Demirjian, Rachael Bade, Josh Dawsey and John Hudson</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>6 a.m.: Trump asserts ‘absolute right’ to investigate corruption</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump on Thursday night asserted an “absolute right” to investigate corruption, which he said includes reaching out to foreign countries for assistance, and suggested that he might sue House Speaker Nancy Pelosi (D-Calif).</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">He comments on Twitter came hours after he told reporters that he would like to see investigations of the Bidens not only by Ukraine but also China, prompting an uproar from congressional Democrats.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“As the President of the United States, I have an absolute right, perhaps even a duty, to investigate, or have investigated, CORRUPTION, and that would include asking, or suggesting, other Countries to help us out!” Trump <a href="https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1179925259417468928">wrote on Twitter</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Later, he took aim at Pelosi for standing by Schiff’s comments in a hearing last week.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump has called for Schiff to resign for remarks in which he embellished Trump’s phone call with Zelensky. Schiff later said his remarks were intended as a parody and that Trump should have recognized that.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Pelosi defended Schiff during an interview with ABC’s George Stephanopoulos that aired Thursday morning on “Good Morning America,” saying his remarks were “fair.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Nancy Pelosi today, on @GMA, actually said that Adam Schiffty Schiff didn’t fabricate my words in a major speech before Congress,” Trump said in <a href="https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1179944461067005952">his tweet</a>. “She either had no idea what she was saying, in other words lost it, or she lied. Even Clinton lover @GStephanopoulos strongly called her out. Sue her?”</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>5 a.m.: Members of Congress getting pressed on developments back home</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">With Congress in recess, House and Senate members are getting pressed on developments in the Ukraine controversy while back home.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Here is <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/video/politics/where-is-the-line-republican-senator-grilled-over-support-for-trump-at-iowa-town-hall/2019/10/03/57406b06-2a76-406e-986a-ce924705cf77_video.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_210">a video</a> of Sen. Joni Ernst (R-Iowa) responding to a constituent Thursday night at a town hall in Templeton, Iowa, who asked a pointed question about the president: “When are you guys going to say, ‘Enough?’”</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>5 a.m.: CNN declines to run Trump campaign ads</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">CNN said Thursday that it will not run two Trump campaign ads because they disparage the network’s journalists and make “demonstrably false” claims while discussing impeachment and pushing unsubstantiated allegations of corruption against Biden.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The network’s decisions come as the Trump administration escalates its attacks on congressional Democrats’ impeachment efforts and continues to lash out at media organizations it tries to discredit as “fake news.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">CNN’s move brought renewed ire from Trump’s reelection campaign, as Communications Director Tim Murtaugh called the news network a “Democrat public relations firm” that “spends all day protecting Joe Biden.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Read more <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/arts-entertainment/2019/10/03/cnn-wont-run-two-trump-campaign-ads-citing-demonstrably-false-claims/?wpisrc=nl_politics&amp;wpmm=1&amp;tid=lk_inline_manual_216">here</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Hannah Knowles</i></p></div></section></div></div><div class="mb-lg pad-bottom-xs pad-top-xs"
